Securities - Only September Futures Were Traded for Public Bonds - Trading Was Very Quiet - Market Prices Fluctuated Very Slightly

Yesterday, at the Chinese Securities Exchange, August futures had already ceased. Only September futures, for one month, were traded on the market. October futures started trading today. The overall environment and news remained in a stalemate. Market sentiment was uncertain, and most people were watching, so trading decreased significantly. Market prices also barely fluctuated. Throughout the day, prices rose slightly at the opening in the morning and fell back slightly at the close. In the afternoon sessions, only Type C and Type D bonds saw some trading. Type D bonds were completely ignored at the opening. The remaining bonds also stagnated at a fluctuation of five fen to one jiao. Therefore, the overall market price result was only slightly better by one or two jiao, and there was no change in the 96. The total transaction volume was only 2,225,000 yuan. The resulting gains and losses are compared and listed on the left (unit: yuan, transaction unit: 100 yuan).

Grains - Shanghai Sales Gradually Become Active - Flour Bounces Back in the Afternoon

Yesterday's flour market started weak and ended strong, forming a revolving situation. After the market opened in the morning, news of foreign wheat reported that Chicago wheat was down 6-7 jiao, Canadian wheat was down 8-9 jiao, and Liverpool wheat was down 1 penny. Initially, the market sentiment remained weak, and both near and far months uniformly fell by about 3 fen. However, after continuous weakness in the downstream markets, the market had already been short for several days, and the floating profits began to generate the intention to cover positions. Customers took advantage of this weakness and successively inquired. By the second session, the market had stabilized. Approaching the afternoon opening, sales of Tianjin gang flour gradually improved, and the spot wheat market also showed signs of improvement. Retail investors emerged and became active, and buying interest suddenly became strong. By the close, the market was smooth all the way, showing a sign of spring returning to the cold valley. As a result, compared to the previous day's closing price, August and September were better by half a fen each, November was better by one fen, December was better by 2.5 li, and January was better by 7.5 li.

New Long Positions in Distant Month Wheat Rise Again - Merchants Give Way, Trading 10,000 Bags of Zhongguan Wheat

After the opening of the wheat futures market yesterday morning, foreign wheat prices uniformly declined, and spot hedging pressure remained strong, with the near-term falling sharply by 8-9 fen. Later, as the flour market rebounded, shorts took advantage of small dips to cover positions. In the afternoon, the market atmosphere gradually became stable, and new long positions were vigorous, especially focusing on the distant months. Therefore, the rebound was stronger than the morning decline, resulting in a situation of rising far months and falling near months. However, after the first session opened for January, the selling interest in the second, third, and fourth sessions was not strong, so the market could not advance further and outwardly fell behind December. As a result of the rise and fall, August was down 6 fen, September was down 3 fen, October and November were each better by 1 fen, December was better by 3 fen, and January was down 5 fen. Zhongguan wheat in the spot market was abundant, and merchants made slight concessions. Yesterday, a total of 10,000 bags were traded. Wuhe wheat was 5.05 yuan, Shaheji wheat was 5.03 yuan, and Mingguang wheat was 5.01 yuan. Other wheat such as Linhuaiguan, Suzhou, Gaoyou, Wuhu, and Hankou wheat ranged from 5 yuan to 4.85 yuan. The higher quality goods remained firm and there were no transactions.

Rice Sales Remain Sluggish - Market Prices Also Show a Gradual Decline

(South Shanghai) Yesterday, a total of 14-15 boats arrived from various gangs, carrying more than 3,000 dan of goods. However, sales in this street market were very low. The Qingdao and Dalian gangs only handled thin transactions of 300-400 bags, and Dongxin handled 50 bags. Therefore, the market situation was difficult to support and showed a downward trend. Houzaogeng rice depreciated by several fen to one jiao, and Baodao rice fell by as much as 1-2 jiao. Duyangjian was weak, but Yinbianyuan was still stable. More than 1,000 dan of Dongxin rice arrived, but sales were not strong, and prices fell again by one chi.

(North Shanghai) Yesterday, about ten boats arrived from various routes in Hexia. Sales of various goods in the market showed slight discounts for Baijing rice, and Yangxianbianyuan high-quality goods were slightly favored, while medium-quality goods were sluggish. Dongxin Jing rice was average, and Dubu Kejian was also weak. Market prices for Baijing high-quality goods were down by slightly less than one jiao, medium-quality goods were down slightly more than one jiao, Yangjianbianyuan high-quality goods were stable and medium-quality goods were down by several fen, Dubu Kejian was also down by slightly less than one jiao, Dongxin Jing was down by one jiao, Baodao rice was lacking in goods and there was no market, and the price of Zhuanqiao Xinjing rice was down by 1-2 jiao.

The New Yellow Soybean Market Situation is Brisk

Since Japanese merchants have been actively sourcing new yellow soybeans in Jiujiang, general market sentiment has become nervous that the source of supply may be obstructed, causing the market to be very tense. Owners of high-quality, dry soybeans are intentionally hoarding them, so medium-quality goods feel even more of an upward pressure. Although the prices opened yesterday were similar to the previous market, the quality was worth 2 jiao. Based on the trend, it seems brisk. Yesterday's transactions included 6,300-400 bags of various Jiujiang soybeans, over 1,000 bags of Changzhou Niupihuang soybeans, and over 700 bags of Hankou Zao Huang soybeans. The sales channels were still oil pressing factories, inland vehicle workshops, and Nanjing local streets.

Silk & Tea - The Price Difference Between Domestic and Foreign Silk is Too Large

Yesterday's overseas silk prices mostly fell, with only a few rises. New York daily silk with uniformity, and Guangdong silk, each fell 3 fen yesterday. Shanghai silk with 7-8 uniformity actually fell 5 fen. Lyon daily silk fell by half a franc, Shanghai silk of AB grades each fell by one franc, and Guangdong silk fell by 0.75 franc. New York near and far term futures, sold at practical prices, rose by one to one and a half fen compared to the previous day. Yokohama rose by about 5 to 6 yuan. The domestic market price is vastly different from overseas silk prices. For example, the B grade of Baichang at 20.22 filaments only fetched a price of 630 yuan, a difference of 3-4 yuan compared to Shanghai sales. Similarly, fine filament (11.13) of Shanghai Baichang silk, such as Fengtai holding a price of 760 yuan, Jinbao at 780 yuan, and Shuangying at 785 yuan, all lacked transactions.

Small Zhenmei Tea Trading is Particularly Brisk - Export of Pulled-Core Zhenmei to Europe is Reviving

Yesterday, according to the Tea Association's report, the green tea market was slightly clearer than last week, but the trading volume of small Zhenmei has been quite brisk in recent days. Yesterday, Xiehe continued to take in over 500 boxes, and Jinlong also slightly followed, with prices similar to before. Zhenmei trading was still sporadic, with Xiehe handling over 100 boxes of tea from the four famous brands, priced at 104 yuan. Baolong imported over 100 boxes of Huizhen, priced at 55 yuan and 65 yuan, and Jinlong imported over 100 boxes of pulled Zhenmei, priced at 106 to 110 yuan. Baitouhang continued to have transactions for Gongxi at 80 yuan. After large quantities of Pingshui tea were sold, the market became quiet last week, with only two batches traded throughout the week, making it the quietest period since the opening of large batches. The report yesterday that large batch trading was smooth was entirely rumored to be unemployed, and is hereby corrected.

Another interview draft stated that, previously, the export of Luzhuang pulled-core Zhenmei green tea had been sluggish due to the war in Morocco. Recently, European sales were said to be still smooth, and Chinese merchants have repeatedly reduced prices to seek sales, with market prices reducing by 20 to 30 yuan compared to before. As a result, the market has become very active. Yesterday, Xiehe, Jinlong, Tongfu, Yongxing and other firms all had large purchases of high-quality goods from Wuyuan and Tunxi, with prices opening at 105 yuan. In addition, needle-shaped Mei tea and pearl tea were also quite popular. Shrimp-eye Mala pearl tea with excellent body was even raised by 2-3 yuan due to the shortage of goods. The green tea market has greatly improved compared to before.

Dried & Salted Goods - Golden Needles and Golden Vegetables Rebounded Sharply - Many Jujubes Arrived, and the Price Fell by One Yuan

Golden Needles - Due to the firm defense of the numbers by the firms, the market has gradually improved and rebounded sharply. Yesterday, the top-grade vegetables opened at 24 yuan, followed by 23.5 yuan to 20.5 yuan, with ordinary vegetables slightly lower. A total of one hundred and several dozen packages were traded, an increase of 1-2 yuan. Market prices have also been raised, and if sales are strong, there may be further increases.

Jujubes - Recently, shipments have arrived from Jiaxing, Hangzhou, Suzhou, Lanxi, etc., and the market has been slightly soft, with a drop of about one yuan. For example, Hangjia, Su and Lanxi's Tutu are all selling for 34 yuan, and the secondary round Lanxi goods are selling for 32 yuan. The usual adjustments are still made.

Black Melon Seeds - Recently, due to the scarcity of arrivals, combined with the lack of inventory in the market and the rise in production prices, opening prices have also gradually increased. Yesterday, over three hundred pieces were opened, with Shuang Gouzi at 15 yuan, Gao Xu Kuizi at 14.6 yuan, secondary Zhuang at 13.6 yuan, and Mingguang Zi at 13.3 yuan.

Sugar Market - Fufubai Ice Sugar's Next Batch is About to Arrive

Yesterday, the market trend remained flat and soft. The association's price for second grade coarse sand white spot goods was 21.7 yuan, and the re-export goods was 6.65 yuan. Dongbai also did not stabilize. Fourth grade white was priced at the original price, and the eighth grade YT mark was 21.13 yuan, with continued transactions. Re-export goods were 6.1 yuan. Ninth grade YR mark spot goods were 20.9 yuan, and re-export goods were 5.9 yuan, both down slightly by one jiao. Number goods, Qing, Chi, and Bai, all demanded the original price and were unwilling to ease up, resulting in a lack of continued opening. Standard Fufubai ice sugar has been in short supply for a long time. Yesterday, the firm telegraphed that the next batch has already been loaded and is en route, and prices are expected to be stable. Piece Goods - Sales of Cotton Cloth Diminish - Factory Prices Also Appear Soft

Yesterday's cotton cloth market, influenced by the continuous weakness in yarn and cotton prices and the decrease in cloth sales, fell one after another. Fine cloth and fine twill from local factories also fell by about 5 fen per bolt. Printed finished goods prices were still stable. Colored cloth and colored twill also fell by about one jiao per bolt. Japanese firms listed Qingdao Gongda Rong, Shuanglongzhu fine cloth, 13.5 pound Shuanglongzhu coarse cloth, and Dakang Factory Wufu Jixiang fine cloth, and Toyota Factory Labashi fine cloth, and Jian Shuangyu fine twill. Yesterday, small amounts of colored goods from Beibang Changjiang inland routes were shipped, and goods from Changzhou and Wuxi were not quiet.

Spring and Autumn

Tidbits

There is a question that hovers in the minds of many of our young people: "Is love something we need?" In fact, if a friend embarks on the path of love and possesses the perseverance to control their environment, they can be considered exceptional. However, the outcome often fails to escape the circle of煩惱(troubles).

The more comfortable one becomes, the more comfort one seeks, and thus laziness surrounds them. We travel on the road of life, with thorns ahead, but life is about struggle. Ignoring the pain of the thorns on our feet, we strive forward. At this moment, there is a beautiful flower blooming with a smiling face by the roadside. Then you immediately become surprised, "I didn't expect that in such a desert-like land, there would be flowers that could comfort my melancholy!" So, from appreciation, to admiration, to plucking it. At this time, you not only forget the pain of the thorns on your feet, but also halt your progress. However, when the flower withers, that is when your pain multiplies. Because you first obtained the comfort of ease, unconsciously forming a habit of laziness, then you have no courage to fight for the difficult future. Instead, they say that everything in society is hypocritical, and what value does a person's life have? Naturally, they fall!

If, in the midst of melancholy, one can obtain a "解語花" (a flower that understands speech) to moisten their dry life and slightly change the environment before them, their spirit will naturally be excited. Under this excitement, if they continue to rush towards their future, singing a song of victory, then everything about them will have a great effect!

Therefore, my conclusion is: love can only be used as a stimulant to excite a melancholy spirit, not as a piece of bread to satisfy hunger. Otherwise, you will definitely be poisoned and die! Moreover, there are many things that our young people need to do right now. Where do we have the free time to indulge in this pink-colored longing!

The Virtue and Grace of Poet Hu Shiyu and His Wife

— Yi Mei

My teacher, Mr. Hu Shiyu, is from Peng Town in Kunshan. He is devoted to learning and practices frugality, admired throughout the country. Along with Gao Chuiwan of Jinshan and Qian Mingshan of Changzhou, he is known as one of the "Three Great Confucian Scholars of Jiangnan." His mother, Madam Cao, was known in the village for her virtuous character. She wore simple clothes and ate simple meals, but she worried about not helping people enough. Two miles northwest of the town, there is a place called Crane Neck Bay. The stone bridge there was destroyed during the Xianfeng era of the Qing Dynasty and was replaced with wood, which was also decayed and broken. Those who carried firewood and vegetables had to take a detour to pass. For thirty years, there were no funds to repair it. Madam Cao wanted to use her private savings to hire workers, but she passed away before she could do so. Therefore, her sons opened her chest and examined the remaining money while weeping, wishing to build this bridge to fulfill their mother's wish. The villagers praised her lasting love and named it "Madam Hu Bridge." An elder named Jin Hewang wrote a record for it and engraved it in stone. Last year, my teacher suffered from erysipelas, and his face and head suddenly swelled, losing all sensation. He was in extremely critical condition. Thanks to the careful treatment of Dr. Chen Zhaochang of Shanghai Hospital, he was able to recover. However, one of his feet was crippled and he had difficulty walking. He had a bamboo sedan chair made, and whenever he recited poetry softly, he would order his servant to carry him to the hibiscus fence and flower garden to enjoy the scenery. Sometimes, he would lean on a dragon-headed cane and, in the slanting sunlight, supervise one or two workers weeding and trimming grass, his old age still full of interest. He often enjoyed exchanging letters and discussing poetry and prose with friends and disciples. Because his hands trembled, his handwriting was crooked, adding to its antique charm. The Guohua Middle School on Gordon Road in Shanghai is renowned for promoting Chinese studies. My teacher donated one thousand yuan to help it as a scholarship fund and invited contemporary literary figures, such as Yan Duhe, Zhou Shoujuan, Gao Chuiwan, Ye Chucang, Hu Puan, Liu Yazi, and Wu Qianan, to serve as graders of the papers. My teacher wrote letters to each of these gentlemen to express his gratitude. I once saw his letter to Chuiwan, which briefly stated: "It has been a long time since I received your instruction, and I often think of you. My hand still trembles and has not fully recovered, and the dampness in my left foot is terribly painful. I am bored in bed, so I wrote a poem to Mr. and your worthy sons each, and I will send them in a painted frame after the autumn cools down. I have recorded the poems below to present to you: 'Two hundred miles apart, not seen for years, a sick old man in a stream house, a hermit poet in a mountain villa, your poetry is refined in the furnace, my painting is frosty and snowy, eagerly awaiting the sound of feathers, boating on the Ming Lake, passing down family learning, how many young people are there now? Letting the younger brothers go out, waiting for the strict parents to work, Jianghai repays friends, literature sweeps away vulgarity, the long sky is clear in autumn, looking eastward to the sea.' Also, I have slightly helped the scholarship fund of Shanghai Guohua Middle School, and there is still the matter of asking you to grade the papers fairly. Principal Wang Yuzhang of Guohua will add a letter to explain it. I hope you will not refuse. I am fortunate to know this in detail because I have recently been teaching at Guohua School."

The Waibaidu Bridge

— Hua Ling

The Waibaidu Bridge in Shanghai can truly be considered one of the most important places in the Public Concession. All those who come to Shanghai from the interior to sightsee, after playing at the Great World, strolling through the City God Temple, climbing to the top of the International Hotel, and paying their respects to the battlefield in Zhabei, must inevitably come to appreciate the Waibaidu Bridge. The Waibaidu Bridge, also known as the Outer Ferry Bridge, is a long and wide iron bridge facing the Huangpu River and spanning the Suzhou Creek. From the surface of the Huangpu River or the Suzhou Creek, looking at it from afar, it truly has the appearance of a "long bridge lying on the waves." How much this "long bridge lying on the waves" weighs and how much it can carry, I am sorry I cannot report. However, since the birth of this bridge, countless wheels and countless feet have passed over it every day, going from south to north and from north to south. Even now, it still lies quietly, tirelessly connecting north and south traffic. Its great endurance can be seen from this.

According to those familiar with Shanghai anecdotes, when the Shanghai Concession was first established, there was not only no large iron bridge at the original site of the Waibaidu Bridge, but there was not even a single-plank bridge. At that time, the only means of transportation between north and south were a few square-headed wooden ferry boats. Therefore, at that time, the place was called "Ferry Crossing." Later, the Concession authorities raised funds to build this large iron bridge, and the general public named it "Ferry Bridge." Initially, vehicles and pedestrians had to pay a "bridge toll" to pass through the bridge. Later, this practice was abolished, so the Shanghai people called it "Baidu Bridge," meaning that one could cross over it without paying a toll. Subsequently, the Zhapu Road Bridge was also built, so everyone called the Zhapu Road Bridge the "Inner Baidu Bridge" and honored the iron-cast Baidu Bridge as the "Outer Baidu Bridge."

One end of the Waibaidu Bridge is connected to the bustling center of Shanghai—the Bund, and the other end leads to the vast Hongkou area, no less than a major throat. On both sides of the bridge stand consulates of various countries, and even more well-known both at home and abroad is the Bund Park, a place that once "forbade dogs and Chinese from entering," now open to the public, located right at the southern end of the bridge, attracting high-class men and women, both Chinese and foreign, from Shanghai all winter, summer, day, and night. Therefore, the Waibaidu Bridge is etched even more deeply in the minds of the general public.

If the Jinpu Railway is the backbone of transportation between north and south in our country, promoting the development of culture, finance, military affairs, industry, and other aspects, then I feel that the Waibaidu Bridge bears a similar mission for Shanghai.

The Mated Mandarin Ducks

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter Five: Double Happiness Arrives, Poem Inscribed on Emerald Leaves; Wedding Dress Surprises as Tried On, Tears Wet the Silk Shawl

Madam Jiang smiled and said, "Even if it's done, you don't have to wear it out right now. It's just to let you try it on." Menglan said, "I'm not wearing it now, what's the point of me trying it on?" Madam Jiang looked at her own daughter, then at the bundles on the bed, thinking to herself, isn't this child being deliberate? With her intelligence, what doesn't she know? So she said, "This isn't my idea either. Your father said that since we have this material, we shouldn't leave it idle at home, so let's make it. After it's made, we can't try it on right away. Trying it on and then putting it away will also set our minds at ease. Because if it doesn't fit, we can have the tailor take it to alter it. You try it on now." As she spoke, she picked up the clothes and walked towards Menglan. With the clothes in her hands, she kept them hanging, not letting go, and looked at Menglan with a constant smile. Menglan saw her mother standing in front of her, acting like a maid serving a young lady. If she completely ignored her, it would be disrespectful to her elder. So she frowned and said, "Mom, why are you in such a hurry? Just give it to me to wear." So she took the clothes and reached out to put them in the sleeves. Madam Jiang grabbed her hand and said, "You can't put on clothes like that. You have to take off the clothes you're wearing before you can put this on." Menglan held the new clothes in her hands for a moment, then nodded and said, "I'll do whatever you say." So she went into the tent and changed her upper body jacket. She lifted the tent and smiled with a frown, "Do you think this looks like a country bumpkin?" Madam Jiang looked her up and down and nodded, "It fits very well. Why don't you just put on the skirt and see how it looks?" Menglan said, "Is there anything wrong with the skirt? There's no need to try it on." Madam Jiang didn't say anything else, but went forward herself, unfolded the folded skirt, held the waistband in both hands, and came to Menglan to tie it on her. Menglan dodged and smiled, "I'm not a three- or two-year-old little girl. You serving me like this is embarrassing me, isn't it?" Madam Jiang said, "Then you put it on yourself." As she spoke, she held the waistband in both hands and still brought it forward. Menglan first sighed deeply, then smiled again. Then she took the skirt and bent over to tie it on herself. She smiled and said, "I'm being obedient in every way, doing what you want, Mom, what else do you want?" Madam Jiang smiled and said, "Why do you always sound angry when you talk?" Menglan didn't say anything, but slowly walked back and forth between the curtains, then looked at Madam Jiang and said, "Have you seen enough, Mom? I can take it off now." Madam Jiang took two steps back, sat on the chair, and looked at her for a long time. (66)

— (Qian Xiaoshan)

Under the blazing sun, the ground is covered in a thousand rays of light. An old woman returns from the field, bent over and still carrying a hoe. I ask her how old she is, eighty plus. Old and shouldn't you rest a little, for your stomach and family, there is no store. Your hair is still not white, from a long time, this principle is not false.

A Record of Unique Skills with Mouth and Nose

— Qing

A few years ago, I saw a performer display his unique skills at a friend's wedding banquet, which made me admire him immensely. What he performed was not some elaborate magic trick that relied solely on tools, but all kinds of exquisite and lively little tricks. However, although they were said to be small tricks, they all relied on his true skill and true ability, without any pretense. His mouth and nose could all help him perform, creating all kinds of patterns. The most interesting thing was that he folded a piece of white paper into a funnel shape with a pointed end and a flat opening, stood it on the tip of his nose, tilted his head back, and spun around a few times. Then he struck a match and started burning it at the opening of the funnel. After a while, the fire had burned away half of the funnel, while the lower half still stood on his nose, without moving at all. Later, it was completely burned to ashes before he ended the trick. Then he supported a small square table with four wooden sticks, put the four stick legs together, and lifted his head to hold them in his mouth. This was not all. He lit four small table lamps and placed them on the table, and in the middle, he put a phonograph, and the Western music record played softly and melodiously. I watched from the side and couldn't help but sweat for him, thinking that the weight on his mouth must be at least several dozen pounds? If it fell, it would be a big disaster. Who knew that he didn't care at all. He also picked up a moon lute in his hand and plucked the strings lightly and casually, playing a Moonlight Serenade from Honolulu, which harmonized well with the Western music in the phonograph record, which was very pleasant to listen to. I didn't expect this clever person to show off his skills. While his mouth was carrying such a heavy burden, he still made sounds in his mouth, beating time for the tune. This made people admire him immensely, and the applause shook the roof tiles. After a tune was over, he put down the moon lute and personally took down the small table lamps and the phonograph from the table one by one. Then he removed the four wooden sticks, pressed on the table with both hands, bowed, and retreated. I saw that this performer's performance was all about working on the center of gravity. He simply understood the theory of the center of gravity in physics very well. It would not be wrong to call him a physicist-performer. Admiring him, I went up to ask him his honorable name. He gave me a business card, which clearly read Qian Bingzhang.

These years, I have been running around for food and clothing, without any desire for entertainment. It has been several years since I saw Qian Bingzhang's unique skills. Yesterday, I read the advertisement for the Sincere Amusement Park in the local supplement of Shen Bao and knew that he was performing at the amusement park. A scholar should be looked at with new eyes after three days of separation, let alone after a few years of separation? I think his mouth and nose skills must have made amazing progress, and he must be able to come up with more new tricks.

Short News: The famous painter Tao Lengyue held an exhibition of paintings in Wumen in early summer. People from the three Wu areas all scrambled to see it quickly. However, Mr. Tao rarely paints fan faces. Therefore, those who like to collect fan faces all regret that they have not obtained a fan painted by Mr. Tao. Now, a friend in Shanghai has asked him to paint one hundred leaves each of landscape and flower fan faces, taking half the price for the painting, six yuan per flower face (original price twelve yuan) and twelve yuan per landscape face (original price twenty-four yuan). The current quota has already reached one hundred pieces. For the convenience of purchasers, he has specially entrusted the manager of Rongbaozhai on Henan Road to display them. Locals can go to choose and purchase in person, and people from other places can remit the painting fee to Tao Lengyue's painting studio at No. 4 Tongyi Lane, Beile Road, and they can get a fan painted by Mr. Tao (fan face included). However, if the quota is full, the original price will still be charged.

Small Knowledge

Common Knowledge About Air Defense

— Ji Yun

Knowledge of air defense has become a necessary common sense for citizens in times of emergency. Therefore, all countries often practice air defense drills, in addition to examining the effectiveness of air defense plans, it is also to practically train citizens on how to deal with enemy aircraft attacks. On July 20, the three cities of Tokyo, Yokohama, and Kawasaki in Japan jointly conducted a large-scale air defense drill, which took four days. The people were very able to show that their knowledge of air defense was not lacking. Looking back at our country, there are still many places where even light control has not been tested.

Air forces always use night attacks as the majority, the most effective of course is air defense, wiping them out halfway. Therefore, the construction of airfields is very important. In large cities, one hundred anti-aircraft guns are distributed, as well as searchlights that hinder enemy aircraft, but it is always inevitable that they can be forced through. For example, in front of sixteen anti-aircraft guns, forty aircraft come, and as many as eight can be forced to intrude. An aircraft can carry a thousand incendiary bombs, so how will the fire trucks in the city cope? The heat of incendiary bombs is about 3,000 degrees, and even steel can be melted. A one-wa bomb is five or six inches in diameter. The largest is twenty watts, and the smallest is only two hundred watts. The Soviet Union announced that ten aircraft can carry 50,000 incendiary bombs. As a result, 9,000 places caught fire, and the others fell in non-fire-prone places, such as roads, parks, and rivers. In this way, within five square kilometers, there are 50,000 bombs, averaging one bomb for every 100 square meters, which is a direct hit.

According to the example of the European War, London used aircraft to defend against air raids, while Paris used anti-aircraft guns. As a result, London shot down more enemy aircraft, but Paris reduced street damage. Britain was attacked by aircraft sixty-three times, and by airships fifty-three times, with 4,821 deaths and injuries. Paris, on the other hand, counted only four six attacks with only about 900 deaths and injuries. Because Britain had no defense methods against the attacks of the Zeppelins.

Poison gas is also a powerful weapon for destroying cities. The gas masks used by the public only cost six yuan each in Japan, and the best ones have the army's seal. The ones used by the army are manufactured by the Chemical Research Institute. The main agent in the gas mask is activated carbon, wrapped in felt. In an emergency, wood charcoal scraps and cotton can also be used, placed in a beer bottle without a bottom. Its effectiveness can only last for a few minutes to several minutes and cannot be called completely effective. The safest thing is to close the house and transform it into a gas-proof residence. Gas masks are only for temporary use when going out.

Five- or six-story wooden houses are easily destroyed by bombs. In large three-story steel-reinforced concrete houses, you can be safe in the basement. The underground passages dug in the Soviet-Shanghai area are probably not very effective under two-story wooden houses. If you don't open up tunnels to the outside, it is even more dangerous. Ordinary houses in our country cannot be said to be bomb-proof. Apart from building dozens of public air-raid shelters, there may not be a first-aid method.

— Dr. Wang Shiying

Before marriage, they engage in excessive masturbation; after marriage, they indulge in sex without restraint. Therefore, their sexual demands have exceeded the limit. Due to the excessive consumption of energy, their spirits decline, their muscles become thin, and they even lose the health of their reproductive glands. All parts of their bodies are greatly hindered, and their health loses its guarantee. Because at this time, the body's blood production is in a normal state, but indulgence without restraint causes excessive consumption of essence and blood, reduces red blood cells, reduces hemoglobin, and greatly threatens the ability to promote metabolism. This is only a slight comparison. There is an even more important relationship, which is the lack of reproductive gland hormone - endocrine. Because sexual desire is generated by endocrine stimulation from the glands and by the reflexive emotions generated by the accumulation of glandular fluid. Therefore, if indulgence is excessive, the secretions produced by the reproductive glands are consumed excessively, and the body and mind are greatly oppressed, which will inevitably lead to abnormal health and shortened lifespan.

As a result of six years of indulgence, his essence was greatly damaged, his face was haggard, his hair was thinning, he had nocturnal emission, spermatorrhea, premature ejaculation, impotence, and a hundred diseases arose. This spring, he was introduced by a fellow patient to take the pure reproductive gland hormone preparation "Reproductin," which immediately presented a picture of abundant spirit and strong physique. After taking four boxes in a row, premature ejaculation and impotence were completely cured. At the same time, nocturnal emission was also cured by taking "Hemet's Semen-Consolidating Tablets."

Knowledge for Couples

— Yao Erchang, MD, Ben Sveni University, USA

Reasons for Infertility and Treatments for Sexual Dysfunction

…Please pay attention to methods for remedying physical and pathological conditions of important organs… …How to enhance sexual function to increase happiness for the future of couples… …Clarify the relationship between the decline of the gonads and this condition, as well as human development

An introduction to physiological knowledge regarding the lives of couples is presented in a well-organized manner. Shen Bao Local Supplement

Talking Point

The Path to "Seeking True Freedom"

— Zi Nan

The newspapers of the 21st carried a Tianjin telegram from Hualian News Agency on the 20th, saying: "In Shihe, Eastern Hebei Pseudo-Area, a People's Self-Defense Army against Yin is discovered, with about a thousand people, all in plain clothes, armed with rifles and Mauser pistols. They have now divided into teams and gone to Funing, Luanxian, Zunhua, Yutian and other places to publicize the expulsion of Yin and contact local militias, using their own guns and strong young men to expand their strength, overthrow the traitor Yin by force, and seek true freedom. The people and militiamen in various places are mostly moved. In recent days, many people have voluntarily joined, and the momentum is growing. The traitor Yin has telegraphed the special police team under his command to search and kill them strictly. At the same time, Yin realized that the old subordinates of Zhang Qingyun and Zhang Yantian had unstable mutiny tendencies, and planned to reorganize them this month."

This news is very simple, but it brings great excitement. I don't know what others feel when they read this telegram, but I was greatly moved.

The sounds of "friendship," "cooperation," and "adjustment" are ringing in our "ears," while acts of aggression, both soft and hard, in the form of military force, economy, culture... are also in front of our "eyes." We do not "judge with our ears," we "listen to their words and observe their actions." As a result, we will certainly not mistake arsenic for honey. Although the enemy hands us "sugar-coated poison" with one hand, the other hand is holding a bright, sharp knife, ready to use it when we refuse their demands. But will that scare us?

The facts of the past few years have clearly answered this point. Under the so-called "benevolence and power combined" of "royal way" and "killing," aren't the volunteers who refuse to be slaves active in the Black Mountains and White Waters? Moreover, in the past few years, in difficult and arduous circumstances, relying solely on their hot blood and earthen guns, haven't they already made the "puppet" and "friendly army" mobilize and run around, restless all day long?

Can some threats make us bow our heads? Can it make us obediently swallow the poison and perish in the enemy's laughter, perishing without resistance!

In this way, in order to survive, it is not surprising that the people of the Pseudo-Area organize the People's Self-Defense Army to "seek true freedom" by "armed force," and that "many people have voluntarily joined in recent days." And on this point, we can confirm what kind of life the people of the Pseudo-Area are living.

I think the line of "seeking true freedom" with "armed force" is correct, and only this road can "seek true freedom." Otherwise, "you reason with the other party, but they use force to solve it. How can a scholar reason with a soldier?" However, there are two things that must be paid attention to in "seeking true freedom" with "armed force." One is not to forget that you are the people, and this struggle is for ourselves, not for the "winner takes all" "king" who "replaces" us. The second is that we should understand that the foundation of victory is built on unity. If we want to compete for credit or be heroes, we will be defeated by the enemy one by one. Moreover, if the unity is not strong, or if there is only unity among a few people, we will still fail. — Naturally, under the common enemy, I say this is somewhat like worrying about something that is unlikely to happen. And I hope this is worrying about something that is unlikely to happen.

Anchoring in Hong Kong at Night

— Xia Lisi

This is truly a sentimental journey.

It was dusk when the ship entered the harbor. The gray sky, the green sea, and the rustling of the waves stirred the traveler's emotions. My uncle Qiu—a kind and generous travel companion—and I stood together on the deck, leaning on the railings and looking at the green mountains on both sides. We allowed the sorrow of parting and resentment to grow continuously in our hearts, and we were silent. The sky grew darker, and the sound of the waves became clearer. The ship's whistle suddenly sounded, awakening us from our dreamlike trance.

"We're almost in Hong Kong," Uncle Qiu said.

"And we're about to part ways," I said.

"There is no banquet in life that does not end in separation," Uncle Qiu was obviously very reluctant to part, but he tried his best to hold back. "Even a flock of goats gets scattered..."

"Can't we prevent the goats from scattering? Can't good friendships disappear?"

"Separation is not the disappearance of friendship; on the contrary, it may be an opportunity to enhance friendship."

"I hope it really is like that!"

As we talked like this, we unconsciously reached the sea off Hong Kong, docking at the Kowloon Pier. The deck was suddenly busy: sailors running back and forth, hotel touts shouting out the names of their hotels. In this clamorous situation, Uncle Qiu prepared the disembarkation procedures, handed the luggage to the hotel people, and turned back.

I stood on the deck, staring blankly at the Hong Kong Peninsula on the opposite shore. The scattered lights on the hillside were so captivating. I, staring at the lights in a daze, was thinking about the creators of these colorful lights—a magnificent and admirable aspect of humanity's conquest of nature. Isn't it true that there is nothing that humanity's power cannot conquer? It's just that I am now bound by a difficult-to-resolve sorrow of parting, and restrained by the handcuffs of emotion. Turning my head, I saw that Uncle Qiu was still standing with me, facing the lights of Hong Kong.

What kind of world must be under those red and green lights! Hong Kong is unfamiliar to me, but I am familiar with Uncle Qiu. Uncle Qiu wanted me to accompany him ashore; the ship would not leave until dawn, and he would take care of me coming back. I agreed. I wanted to see what Hong Kong really looked like...

The small ferry took Uncle Qiu and me to the shore of Hong Kong.

The seaside road in Hong Kong was quiet and clean, with the southern monsoon blowing at the end of July. Several rickshaws came over, soliciting business. But Uncle Qiu said:

"We should walk."

The roads in Hong Kong are not easy to walk; especially when walking up the slopes, it is a bit tiring. Uncle Qiu knew that we should find a place to rest; at this time we were a little hungry, so we went to a restaurant together.

I will never forget that delicate and charming waitress. Although I didn't know her name or anything about her, she warmed my heart during the journey. We drank cup after cup of double-distilled wine. The weather was still hot, and sweat kept pouring out. She turned on the electric fan and often brought us fragrant towels.

"Where are you two gentlemen going? To the provincial capital?" she asked in a gentle, melodious Cantonese.

"I teach here," Uncle Qiu replied, and pointed to me and said, "He is going to the provincial capital, as you said."

"The provincial capital is at its liveliest now—" she stood beside me, opening her eyes as if she saw a place she was familiar with, "Picking lychees in a small sampan, facing the stars on a summer night, you will feel an indescribable pleasure. Perhaps a walk along the Bund will make you feel that the world is not as gloomy as pessimists say..."

"What about Hong Kong? Why don't you miss Hong Kong?" I said.

"Because the banks of Lychee Bay have nurtured my youthful love... But now, sir, the evil hand of life has strangled my throat!"

We spent more than an hour in front of this eloquent waitress. When we left, I still cast her a nostalgic glance, and she smiled charmingly.

Hong Kong, why do I have to leave you?

At two o'clock that night, I still couldn't fall asleep, so I groped up from the cabin to the deck to bid farewell to this beautiful island. The lights had dimmed, leaving only a few sparse ones, flickering and smiling. At this time, I didn't know if Uncle Qiu had fallen asleep yet. And I thought of that delicate waitress. God, I am deeply blessing her!

Sea and the Old Man

— Luo Peng

One bright afternoon, I moved alone to this seaside to live in solitude. I love the sea: the sea has left too deep an impression on me. It can agitate my nerves and even make me melancholy.

Every day, when the sunlight at the end of the sea is about to sink below the western horizon, I sit in my simple

Page 20

wooden house, always staring blankly out of the small square window, watching the sea put on its beautiful evening gown: two or three small birds, leisurely circling over the sea, as if wanderers searching for a place to return; at the end of the sea and sky, a light purple haze rises. Fishermen, sailing small boats, smoothly ride the breeze, dispersing the mist, sailing on the shimmering sea at dusk, the bow cutting through the calm sea surface, as light as a swallow skimming the water. In a moment, the night will cover my window.

Perhaps the scenery at dusk is too beautiful, and sitting by the small window still cannot satisfy my desire for enjoyment. Or perhaps there is something else outside that attracts my attention more? Taking advantage of the sun not yet setting, I go for a walk on the beach.

At the seaside, I saw an old man, who at first did not catch my attention, but gradually his lonely figure and the sea at dusk occupied my mind. He was so weak: every day, every day, he dragged his slow steps, bent over, weakly tapping the sand with his cane, stumbling to the beach, where he sat down on a round green stone. The traces of his cane and his steps were imprinted on the beach, dragging a long tail, extending all the way to the distant, unseen part of the beach...

His excessive solemnity startled me, making me afraid to approach him, only daring to watch him from afar. The old man quietly gazed at the distance of the sea, as if there was an incomprehensible secret in front of him.

As days passed, this strange old man became more familiar in my impression. I was no longer as afraid to approach him as before. I tried to talk to him, I stared at him, but he ignored me, as if he didn't feel anything at all.

When the sunlight was just flashing the last rays of the day at the end of the sea and sky, and the dark hand of darkness was about to grip the earth tightly, the old man's deeply sunken, dry eye sockets would, as usual, be rolling with crystal clear tears. Several times, I was inexplicably moved by the old man to tears as well. Every day was like that, the seaside was so quiet that only the sound of waves lapping the beach could be heard, and the old man would still drag his slow steps back to his original path.

Finally, I vowed that I would understand the old man's story. So, I closely followed behind him.

About a hundred steps from the sea, on a high slope, was the old man's residence—a dilapidated hut worn down by wind and rain year after year. Before the old man returned to the house, at the door of this house, there was a middle-aged woman in her thirties, sitting there blankly waiting. In front of her was a lunch basket.

The old man opened the lock on the door, the middle-aged woman put the lunch basket on a small table, and then turned around and walked out of the house, without saying a word. The old man never paid any attention to her.

One day, before the old man returned to his house, I asked this middle-aged woman, inquiring about the old man's story: "Excuse me, what is this old man to you?"

"He is my father!"

"Then why don't you talk to him every day?"

"Alas! He doesn't like us women. He likes sons. He says daughters are all debt collectors!"

"Then does he have sons?"

"He has sons, he has two sons. My eldest brother went to a very, very far place on the other side of the sea eight years ago. He said he went to make money. He said he would come back the next year, but, alas..." She wiped away her tears with the corner of her clothes: "He hasn't come back until now. Some people say he joined the army and was killed on the battlefield. Some even said he sent a letter back, telling us not to miss him, but my father doesn't know this news yet!"

"Then what about his second son?"

"My second younger brother?" She raised her head, opened a pair of desolate eyes, and glanced at me: "Alas, it was the year before last, the year before last, he went out to fish and encountered a big storm and was swept away by the waves. His body hasn't been found until now..." As she spoke, she began to cry mournfully.

In the distance, the sound of the old man's cane tapping on the beach reached our ears, tapping on our hearts with each tap.

Under the Sunlight (Continued)

— Shu

Under the sun, they still run desperately for their own livelihood: one has to "collapse one day, that would be good."

Searching, searching, on the street, somewhere there is an open space, even if sweat flows like a spring, it is enough to excite them to spin around. Children play piercing gongs and drums, a set of flower spears, a set of dog iron rings, a set of lotus ballads... Under the hot sun, people are so hot that they are about to faint. When the police come to interfere, they also send the coppers thrown down by the first few spectators as "cigarette money." With the remaining dozen or so coppers, how can the family of three survive?

Middle-aged Lao Guan became anxious and forgot about the scorching sun. Like a mad dog, he begged, begged, caring about the coppers on the ground, which were so few that people dared not look, dared not think about, those few coppers.

"What about today's life? What about life?" Thinking of this, his heart turned cold, but he still had to beg hard, attracting applause, attracting laughter...

He was out of breath, his face turned pale. The child looked scared and said softly, "Dad, take a rest, let us do it."

"No, no! One more time, and someone will throw coppers."

Still begging like a mad dog, the sun scorching like fire, fewer and fewer people watching, but what about the money? The money collected had already been given to the police, and what about this day, this day...

A burst of dizziness, everything went black before his eyes, Lao Guan really fainted involuntarily. The passersby became agitated, the child cried empty-heartedly, someone gave him ten drops of Huoxiang Zhengqi water, but it was useless, saying that he had heatstroke and it was too deep, it was over...

It was over, which was ultimately good. In this era, Lao Guan had indeed reached the end of the road, and now, he finally collapsed, in front of life, under the sunlight.

Lotus Lantern

— Meng Hua

Old woman Shi woke up drenched in cold sweat. She rubbed her blurry eyes and looked at everything in the room distrustfully. Although it was not yet light, everything looked so familiar to her that she suddenly realized that she had just had a nightmare.

She vaguely saw her son kneeling in front of her bed, wearing a short jacket soaked in blood, begging her in a sorrowful voice.

"Mom, I'm suffering so much now! Give me some pocket money to spend. If you have enough money, please ask a craftsman to make me a set of clothes, this blood-soaked short shirt and pants are too embarrassing! I have suffered enough in the underworld, people are abusing me, saying that I am a poor ghost..."

Old woman Shi recognized that this was her son who had died not long ago. She just wanted to reach out to touch him and ask him where he came from, but suddenly, the rooster crowed in the next room, and he ran out of the window in a panic. Old woman Shi just wanted to hold on to him, but because she used too much force, she didn't catch him and instead fell down herself.

She didn't fall to the ground. This was a dream, she was still lying in bed. Now she woke up. The corners of her eyes were still wet, and she muttered to herself in a low voice:

"What's wrong, is Long'er returning to life? Sigh, he really has suffered enough. Since he died, I only burned four hundred silver ingots for him. How is that enough for him to spend? He has no relatives in the underworld..." Perhaps because the fifteenth of July was approaching, her son gave her a dream, asking her to chant scriptures for him so that he could be reborn. Her son was good by nature, she thought in her heart, but he followed bad companions and committed a murder, so he couldn't be reborn.

She immediately thought of something that happened a year ago. Her son used to sell snacks at the entrance of the village. At that time, she herself was suffering from a bad illness and didn't have money to hire a doctor, which made him very anxious. On that day, she still remembered clearly, it was the thirteenth day of the sixth lunar month, before dawn, he got up, his face pale, and ran to the bed anxiously to tell her:

"Mom, I need to go to the city. I'll be back early in the morning. Maybe I can ask a doctor from the city to come to the village..."

Movie

Miscellaneous Notes on (Little Sisters)

"Little Sisters" tells the story of a young girl named Lin Manli who lives with her stepmother, Ms. Li, and her sister, Manna. The stepmother treats her harshly, abusing and bullying her in every way, and she always favors her own daughter, Manna. Therefore, Manna becomes even more arrogant and intimidating, viewing her sister, Manli, as a thorn in her side, and driving her like a servant. Manli is in such a situation, simply like an animal, spending her days in tears, yet lacking the ability to resist, so she can only cry in vain. Her pitiful experience and her difficult situation are enough to make the viewers shed tears of sympathy. The saying "the sun in autumn, the fist of the stepmother" is proven here to be true and not just empty talk.

Little Oolong Yuan Meiyun plays both roles of the gentle Manli and the spoiled Manna mentioned above. One day, when filming several scenes of Manna slapping Manli in the face, Huang Jiamo, who was watching from the side, found it amusing and said to Yuan Meiyun: "Miss Yuan, aren't you just slapping yourself in the face?" Although this is a joke, the meaning contained in his words is indeed very profound. How exactly Yuan Meiyun is slapping herself in the face, this ingenious photography technique is indeed worth watching.

Xu Qinfang made a comeback this time, guest starring in the role of the stepmother. She is indulgent and doting towards Manna, but strict and mean towards Manli. Therefore, in this play, she constantly uses two extremely opposite faces, that is, a standard stepmother who is extremely fierce. And her performance is "indeed" very good, tightly grasping the identity of the character in the play, making the audience's sense of injustice and resistance unable to be extinguished even after three days.

In summary, "Little Sisters" is a family tragedy, but on the other hand, the satirical humor mixed in is also very rich. Therefore, although it can make people cry sadly, it can also make people laugh, laugh until their stomachs hurt and tears flow.

Little Singer Babe Bai Ling in "Liyuan Thinks of Her Son"

Great Shanghai Presents Tonight at 9:15 PM

News of (Our Children's Theater) Preparation

The twentieth century not only discovered the power of the people; but children have also begun to understand the true self-help movement, to fight against all those who deny children's abilities and oppress children into becoming slaves. Especially in this cry for national salvation, progressive children have recognized their abilities—the same "human" abilities as adults—and are prepared to unite into a vast and powerful children's front, standing on an equal footing with adult groups, and holding hands tightly with all truly revolutionary and progressive adult groups. Now, receiving the news of the establishment of the "Our Children's Theater Preparatory Committee" proves that the children of the twentieth century have indeed bravely jumped out of the "attached" prison, broken free from the shackles of slavery, and appeared in this stormy era with a new posture, becoming fighters on the revolutionary front.

From the name "Our Children's Theater," it can of course be understood that this children's theater is not art for art's sake, or selfish individualistic play, but belongs to the vast "us"—belongs to the new bright society, a part of the collective power of the people.

Now, the "Our Children's Theater Preparatory Committee" still feels that there are not enough talents; and in order to gather the many progressive children scattered everywhere, so that the organization of the society can be more sound and the cadres more solid, it is specially seeking comrades publicly (under sixteen years old, over thirteen years old). It is hoped that all progressive children will automatically and bravely participate. And please, gentlemen who care for children, after receiving the news of their seeking comrades, immediately pass it on to progressive children. Participants should first send a letter to Haiyan Theater, No. 7 Huatongfang, North Xizang Road Bridge, or to Lu Jing, No. 50 Jishanli, Kangnuot Road, Kangnuo Village. Or go directly to Haiyan Theater to talk to He Tuoxin face to face (time: 3 PM to 8 PM daily), or go to No. 50 Jishanli to talk to Lu Jing face to face (time: morning daily).
